Excellent care !  I just adopted a tiny deaf white Persian kitty who has had multiple medical problems her whole life.  Many requiring surgery and many needing long term care. Daisy is frightened of anyone touching her, and any vet care at all is just plain hard to do. Her Persian fur was the worst matted mess I have ever seen. If you want good care and a deeply knowledgeable  Doctor to care for your pet.  This is the place !!</Text>

<Text>Be careful taking your pets here! They're more interested in selling services than your companions well being. They wanted to hospitalize my puppy for an upset stomach after testing negative for parvo. When I declined hospitalization they wanted to charge me $115 for blood work but could not tell me what they were testing for. Customer service leaves a lot to be desired as well. I had to stand at the desk for way too long without being acknowledged by the receptionist while she spoke to a vendor on the phone. Total waiting time in the room was almost 2 hours. This does not include a 20 minute lecture by the vet tech about what a bad puppy owner I am. They wouldn't even let me out of the room to pay for the services, made me wait while they ran my card. And even asked me not to let Stella's paws touch the floor on the way out! I went to another vet in Sacramento for a second opinion. He advised me to feed Stella rice, cottage cheese, yogurt and canned pumpkin for 2 days. Add chicken the 3rd day. And begin mixing in her puppy food after that. He also advised administering pepto-bismal with a syringe to settle her stomach and mix pedialyte with her water for dehydration. Wish I had gone to him first. I would have saved almost $100 for an unnecessary fluid IV (which I practically had to administer myself) and an anti-nausea injection. I wonder how many clients would have followed this vet's first recommendation to hospitalize my 7 week old puppy. And to the vet tech with the pit bull with skin allergies and neurotic Labrador that destroys your furniture when you don't exercise her because she's afraid of the rain who lectured me.....please read this. "The primary and most important time for puppy socialization is the first three months of life. During this time puppies should be exposed to as many new people, animals, stimuli and environments as can be achieved safely and without causing overstimulation manifested as excessive fear, withdrawal or avoidance behavior. For this reason, the American Veterinary Society of Animal Behavior believes that it should be the standard of care for puppies to receive such socialization before they are fully vaccinated." I would add that many skin problems in dogs are caused by stress that can be alleviated with proper exercise. And your lab wouldn't tear up your furniture if you exercised her daily (and that doesn't mean a simple walk around the block when the sun is shining) And who ever heard of a Labrador being afraid of the water??! She's afraid of the rain because you never take her out to play in it! But what do I know? I'm no vet. But I don't appreciate the lecture or the attempt to extort my hard earned dollars for unnecessary and psychologically damaging treatment like leaving a 7 week old puppy in a cage overnight because she's slightly dehydrated from a mild case of a sore tummy. I will never set foot in this establishment again and I would advise anyone reading this to seek treatment elsewhere< /Text><userid>103549489339599087211< /userid></record>

The content of the course are interesting and the videos are easy to follow. Every week ends with a quiz, an assignment that needs to be completed and you're also required to review your peers in the class. <review>Machine learning Class sucked.  This was the second awful experience I had with coursera:  MongoDB class was also impossible to complete.

Navigating the site is a pain as there is such a high latency that any click I made took so long to respond that frustration was immediately the result of navigating the coursera site and course pages.  Videos played but would automatically bypass their built-in quizzes and just play the videos without allowing me to perform the quiz portion, so it was impossible to determine if I was on the correct path.

Video's that were useful were impossible to navigate as attempting to fast forwarding or rewind to a previously watched section was nearly impossible... the settings bar never(or, hardly ever... i had to reload the page if i wanted to move around in the video because watching the videos made my browser wholly unresponsive...) shows and makes it impossible to navigate the videos.  The pause/unpause function work fine, just navigating is frustratingly slow. I gave up on watching the vector videos over and over... they were not that informative and did not have any real content, so watching them over and over was a waste of my time.  long, and drawn out 15 minute video's could have been bypassed with a printout that could be read and fully comprehended in ~10-15 seconds, and speeding up the videos using the speed setting makes the web pages completely un-navigable.

the quizzes are a joke: repeat the same questions over and over until you get the correct answers.  If you do not get the correct answers, there are no methods for you to learn what you did wrong: you are only told that you provided a wrong answer and re-directed to watch the same videos which you obviously did not understand in the first place- over and over again- until you "do" "get it", which for me was never.

<Review>Finally got around to trying Luisa and Sons in Cerritos. They're situated in strip lot on South Street, next to Cafe 86. It's a small bakery serving up classic Filipino pastries and desserts like egg pie, cassava, turon, sponge cake mamon and many more. What caught my eye was their display case of hopia which I heard was good. They have several selections on hand like mung bean, red bean, ube and baboy (made out of pork fat, candied winter melon and green onions).

I decided to try a dozen ube hopia (85 cent each) and half dozen chicken empanadas. The chicken empanadas were tasty and crust was on point, but unfortunately their ube hopia was a complete disappointment. The ube flavor was lacking and quality of crust wasn't flaky. Both essential characters to good hopia. it just tasted like standard pastries without any soul and originality.

All in all, the experience was okay. The hopia place near my house is so much better. Return visit is unlikely, but if you decide to come here anyways skip the ube hopia.

Note: For some nutritional facts, mongo or mung bean helps lower blood cholesterol levels, helps prevent breast cancer and also it has low sugar level. So if ever you are on a strict diet, this hopia mongo will surely be a good pick. Make sure to mention that to your doctor. Hahaha!<//Review><user_name>valen zuela<//user_name><GmapID>0x80dd2da0558bc355:0xf7e3751ef5e18aff<//GmapID>< date>

<Date>1416199019771<//Date><rate>4<//rate><Pictures>None</Pictures>< Text>
Lotta empanada for da dolla, I holla!

Just $0.60 gets you one of these bad boys, the Pilipino chicken empanada
Flaky, sweet, savory & oh so delicious!  Tender pieces of chicken, carrots and raisins stuffed inside a buttery crust.  I can polish off about 75 of these during one sitting ;p

Luisa & Sons is a Pilipino bakeshop offering traditional cuisine from the homeland, both savory & sweet.

Fresh baked goods are prepared daily & gobbled up by the masses

Have a sweet tooth?  No problem!  Luisa & Sons offers delectable treats to satisfy your sugar fix

Besides the sweets & baked goods, savory dishes are available for purchase in the freezers and for pre-order food trays, such as sisig & dinuguan.  My family has often ordered a tray of pancit malabon (Pilipino noodle dish) & a box of empanadas for special occasions.  They're always a hit & nary a leftover afterwards.

Service has always been good.  I'm a regular, so the staff already knows they have to restock their supplies once I'm done shopping ;p

Parking is in the Unimart shopping plaza, shared with Milk & Honey, Azon & Canaan restaurants, among others.

What da bloody heck ya waitin for?  Go to Luisa & Sons Bakeshop already!

Highly recommend!

NOMNOMNOMNOMNOMNOMNOMNOMNOMNOMNOMNOM< /Text>

<Name>Jaime Marron</Name>< Review>
So far I've been to this place 8-10 times having experienced 3 different barbers out of the 6 or so and have had OUTSTANDING service. I'm very particular about my haircuts and before this place would almost always personally fix my haircut once I get home. But this place is cheaply priced ($9-12 for me before tip, Fresno can be $16 for haircuts, I'm used to $10 back home), usually very little wait time, open 7 days a week. They take their time and deliver. Andy seems to be the most wanted barber and I have yet to have a cut from him but once more they all seem to be pretty awesome.<//Review>

This was the Worst Fast Food Experience ever! (I'm Black and this incident was racially charged.)
Me and my girlfriend walk in and sit down to read the menu, then IMMEDIATELY the Manager yells at us from across the room "If you're going to sit here, then go sit outside"
So I told said "Okay" and proceeded to look at the menu then she stared at us (and mind you an elderly lady walked in right before us and the manager only asked her one time if she was still looking at the menu, but the manager stared at us and asked us multiple times "Do you know what you want yet?" Clearly all of us were still looking at the menu deciding.
Now I fear SPIT or something more DISGUSTINGLY will be in my food IF I order again.
# Drive thru # burrito # prices</review>
